  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2cb1d985-13d6-4ba4-9158-4d5812fe17fa'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer10791691246092584648">MasterSinger Merelan and Harper Petiron were a brilliant and devoted couple. Merelan was the most outstanding soprano ever heard on Pern, and was often the only one who could master Petiron's technically accomplished compositions. When, after a long and difficult birth, Robinton was born to them, it should have been the culmination of a unique partnership.<br/><br/>But Petiron, almo</span>
  <span id="freeText10791691246092584648" style="display:none">MasterSinger Merelan and Harper Petiron were a brilliant and devoted couple. Merelan was the most outstanding soprano ever heard on Pern, and was often the only one who could master Petiron's technically accomplished compositions. When, after a long and difficult birth, Robinton was born to them, it should have been the culmination of a unique partnership.<br /><br />But Petiron, almost from the first day, had no time for his son, refusing to see the incredible talent the boy possessed, ignoring his achievements and maintaining a strict and disapproving vigilance over him at all times.<br /><br />Carefully, secretly, the Harper Hall took over, training the greatest talent Pern had ever seen - a talent that was more than just musical, for Robinton was able to talk to the dragons of Pern.<br /><br />As constant sadness beset his personal life, so a startling career sent him like a meteor through the Holds and Weyrs of Pern until, as MasterHarper, he became part of the great plan to rescue Lessa from the brutal rule of Holder Fax - Lessa, who was to be the saviour of the dragons of Pern.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10791691246092584648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_5502715" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5502715" />
    <a title="Ryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/331867-ryl"><img alt="Ryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1191119311p2/331867.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5502715?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryl" href="/user/show/331867-ryl">Ryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345424600" href="/book/show/471562.The_Masterharper_of_Pern">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/331867-ryl?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/331867-ryl?shelf=thissucked">thissucked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/331867-ryl?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5502715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6749207596317119200">I've figured out why Anne McCaffrey frequently stated that the Pern novels should be read in publication order rather than by their internal chronology. It's because she couldn't be arsed to keep accurate notes about the series and didn't want her readers to catch on to that fact by noticing the errors. <br/><br/>My favorite example of this is the rapid progress of Piemur and Jancis' relationship. At the end of <i>The Renegades of Pern</i> they finally slept together for the first time. Then the workers at Landi</span>
  <span id="freeText6749207596317119200" style="display:none">I've figured out why Anne McCaffrey frequently stated that the Pern novels should be read in publication order rather than by their internal chronology. It's because she couldn't be arsed to keep accurate notes about the series and didn't want her readers to catch on to that fact by noticing the errors. <br><br>My favorite example of this is the rapid progress of Piemur and Jancis' relationship. At the end of <i>The Renegades of Pern</i> they finally slept together for the first time. Then the workers at Landing woke up the Deus in Machina who told them the story of <i>Dragonsdawn</i>. In the first few chapters of the next book, <i>All the Weyrs of Pern</i>, someone asks Piemur when the wedding will be. Because it's been all of a couple of days and they're engaged now. There's something to be said for seducing your girlfriend in the horse pasture, it seems.<br><br>At first glance, you wouldn't expect Master Robinton to be a continuity error. He's one of McCaffrey's favorite boyfriends (along with Prince Jaxom the Annoying) and appears in every book set in the Ninth Pass. She seemed to have a pretty good grip on his timeline. At least she did until she decided to write <i>The Masterharper of Pern</i> and warp his entire life into unrecognizability.<br><br>What are the facts about Robinton's life pre-1998? We can't ask McCaffrey because she's dead, but her answers would probably be a little iffy even if she were alive. So let's ask someone who's read more Pern novels than she should admit to. That would be me. Hi. <br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430344249i/14705794.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>Master Robinton was the leader of the Harper Hall in the late Second Long Interval/Early Ninth Pass. His father was Petiron, who ended his days working at Half-Circle Sea Hold which was conveniently located as far away from the Harper Hall as he could get. Robinton's preferred wine was Benden red, which helped save his life when he had a heart attack at the queen's open mating flight at Ista Weyr. He ended his days at Cove Hold on the Southern Continent where he, D'ram, and Lytol were in charge of the excavations at the ancient Landing site. He died along with his fire lizard Zair and Aivas after the highly improbable events of <i>All the Weyrs of Pern</i>. He was an older gent, most likely in his fifties at the beginning of <i>Dragonflight</i> which means he was around 70-80 when he died. On the whole he was a likeable character, a fatherly figure to the harpers, a steadfast friend to the Weyrs, a man who was passionate about gathering and disseminating knowledge to everyone.<br><br>And then <i>Masterharper of Pern</i> comes along to stomp all over that last statement. <br><br>The first grand offense against continuity committed by this novel is having Robinton's mother be a member of the Harper Hall. Who remembers why Menolly was such a big deal when she became an apprentice harper? All together, class: It was because girls were not accepted as Harpers! In the early Pern novels a woman's lot was not a fulfilling one for ladies with career ambitions. Most women were wives and mothers; the lucky ones who were Searched were able to do more with their lives than be brood mares. This is an example of McCaffrey trying to retcon Pern into some kind of utopia which is a big reason why all the novels after the first half of <i>Renegades of Pern</i> sucked. <br><br>But I can deal (barely) with Mastersinger Merelan. McCaffrey begins to attempt to explain why the number of women in the Hall dropped to zero near the end of the book, but the problem is she spent too much time on the bullshit at the beginning when she turned Robinton into the prototype Golden Child. For you see, my friends, young Robinton was a child prodigy who could play every instrument perfectly by the time he was three, who could write music when he was five, who rewrote the Teaching Ballads, and also sang the Question Song for the Benden Weyrleaders. (Astute readers will recall that in <i>Dragonflight</i> Robinton clearly stated that he had just rediscovered this ballad before he sang it to Lessa.) <br><br>Just to cram his wonderfulness down our throat even more, McCaffrey adds daddy issues. Petiron was so wrapped up in his composing and his wonderfully gifted soprano wife that he just didn't have the time to care about his son. He basically ignored Robinton for the first five or six years of his life, which sent Robinton straight into a borderline unhealthy relationship with his mother. The majority of the book deals with this. Because that's what we really wanted to know about the Masterharper, right? We wanted to hear—in excruciating detail, no less—all about the freaky weird love triangle between Merelan, Petiron, and Robinton. The one that ended up with Petiron and Robinton arguing over who loved her more after she died? Yeah, that one.<br><br>The second major continuity error comes when young Robie first meets a dragon. He's able to talk to it. Astute readers once again may remember that Robinton couldn't hear dragons until he had his heart attack and Ramoth and Mnementh started talking to him to keep him alive. After that he heard them a couple more times, but only when they contacted him directly. (These same astute readers will also remember that only powerful queen riders like Lessa could hear all dragons in addition to their own. Men could only talk to their own unless circumstances warranted, like the heart attack.)<br><br>With the introduction of dragons comes the name-dropping segment. Robinton meets every single person who's important in the later Pern novels. He runs into young Raid, later Lord Holder of Benden when he's just a stuffy youth. His best friend is young Falloner who later becomes F'lon, father of F'lar and F'nor. He encounters C'gan, later known as the first rider to die of Threadscore in the Ninth Pass. He works at High Reaches for a while where he meets and immediately dislikes Fax. In later chapters he sees Lessa as a toddler in a scene that's not completely shoehorned in at all.<br><br>Oh and while I'm thinking of it, McCaffrey rips off Menolly's table-walking scene at the end of <i>Dragonsinger</i> for Robinton's own promotion to journeyman. At fifteen, which was supposed to be obscenely young. Because going back and checking on Menolly's age at her own promotion (14) would be too hard. <br><br>Then there's the pointless marriage that's only there to add some tragedy to Robinton's life (as if this hatchet job disguised as a novel wasn't tragedy enough). He meets Kassia at High Reaches and immediately falls in love with her like every other guy in the Hold. However, none of the others are Mr. Perfect Robinton, so they can't make her forget her dead husband and fall for them. But, alas, they decided that they should go on a late autumn cruise for their honeymoon. I would like to point out that Kassia was a sailor raised in a family of sailors. This is important because late autumn is a dangerous time to be out on open water in northern climes. You would think someone with sailing in her blood would know that. Even <b>I</b> know that and my family hasn't been on the water in three generations.<br><br>Long story short, the newlywed couple runs into one of these dangerous autumn storms and Kassia catches a chill which later kills her. Robinton gets mopey and goes back to the Harper Hall where he ends up working with the Masterharper until his inevitable promotion. <br><br>And this is where the real story should begin. Fax is taking over the northwest, hold by hold, and the other Lord Holders are doing nothing. F'lon is killed in a fight that is completely ripped off from the climactic wedding knife fight in <i>Dragonquest</i> (it's even at the same flippin' <i>Hold</i> for cryin' out loud!) and the Weyr folds in on itself. Fear grips the continent as society begins a slow, downward spiral. This is the kind of situation that breeds heroes. What is Bargen, future Lord Holder of High Reaches doing as he hides with his supporters in the abandoned High Reaches Weyr? How are F'lar and Mnementh doing over in Benden as they chafe against R'gul and Jora's mismanagement? Why won't the other Lord Holders join forces against Fax? How does the Harper Hall deal with all these issues in their role as the mediating and educating force of society? What's up with the spies?<br><br>Hell if I know. The meat of the story is handwaved away so that we can get to the gristle masquerading as juicy bits. Like, did you know that Robinton was actually Camo's father? But he couldn't love his birth son because Camo was a little slow and therefore not smart enough to warrant paternal love or attention. (The obvious parallels to Petiron are simultaneously ham-handed and ignored by our Lady Author which is a feat I wouldn't have believed if I hadn't read it with my own eyes.) But then Sebell comes along and Robinton transfers all his fatherly affection to him. For you see, Sebell is the son of Robinton's mother's cousin. This is clear when he demonstrates the family tendency towards annoying precocity. (He also steals Menolly's multiple pipes several years before she made them on the other side of the continent.)<br><br>The novel finally grinds to a halt when Robinton gets word that dragonriders are going to Ruatha hold. In a moment of blinding imbecility, he decides that he's going to disguise himself as a drudge so he can see what's going to happen. How did he know something was going to happen? Apparently precognition comes with the title of Masterharper. <br><br>This is the point where I uttered a vile profanity and closed the book. Do yourself a favor, pretend the Pern series ends after <i>Dragonsdawn</i>. You'll save yourself a lot of heartbreak.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6749207596317119200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6919194152070010589">I remember Robinton, Masterharper of Pern always being one of my favorite characters. Rereading this just emphasized that fact. This is the story of his life from a newborn until a bit after he becomes the Masterharper of Pern.<br/><br/>He is an incredible character with a wonderful story.   <span id="freeText6919194152070010589" style="display:none">I remember Robinton, Masterharper of Pern always being one of my favorite characters. Rereading this just emphasized that fact. This is the story of his life from a newborn until a bit after he becomes the Masterharper of Pern.<br /><br />He is an incredible character with a wonderful story. His mother and father are both talented musically, which enhances the musical talent in him that he is a prodigy. He is close with his mother and really has no relationship with his father. His father is jealous of him because of the time he takes with his mother. The people in the Harper Hall pretty much all raise him. He turns out to be an incredible person, an amazing talent and one who can speak to dragons.<br /><br />He goes through a lot as he grows up and the story is never dull. I thoroughly enjoyed this one and am looking forward to the coming books. It definitely brought back all the love I had for these books. The previous books were alright, but this one shows the real talent of Anne McCaffrey and why the stories of Pern are so captivating and loved.</span>

<div id="review_105554373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105554373" />
    <a title="Doreen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1235896-doreen"><img alt="Doreen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348630486p2/1235896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105554373?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doreen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doreen" href="/user/show/1235896-doreen">Doreen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345424600" href="/book/show/471562.The_Masterharper_of_Pern">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105554373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6781685560823776256">I've realized that Ms McCaffrey's books offend me in exactly the same way the Sex and the City movies offend me: that the main characters and their dysfunctional relationships are supposed to be somehow sympathetic, if not outright aspirational. In this book, Robinton himself is less obnoxious than her usual main character (even if I thought the one scene where he compared holding his mom to holding his wife really Freudian and gross,) but Merelan is excessively odious: trying to hide his talent</span>
  <span id="freeText6781685560823776256" style="display:none">I've realized that Ms McCaffrey's books offend me in exactly the same way the Sex and the City movies offend me: that the main characters and their dysfunctional relationships are supposed to be somehow sympathetic, if not outright aspirational. In this book, Robinton himself is less obnoxious than her usual main character (even if I thought the one scene where he compared holding his mom to holding his wife really Freudian and gross,) but Merelan is excessively odious: trying to hide his talents from his horrible father (and there's another terrible relationship the author champions) but getting upset with said father when he doesn't realize the boy's potential. The worst bit was when, offended that Petiron couldn't remember their son's age, she took the kid and ran off to another hold for months. Screw being an adult and actually talking about your problems with your mate. Run away, and all your problems will be solved.<br /><br />Oh, and don't get me started on the treatment of Hallana. My views on spanking aside, the fact that her father, who'd spoiled her her entire life, decides that he's finally going to raise his hand to her when she's an adolescent, and then have this treatment be effective, beggars belief.<br /><br />I am so glad I am through with McCaffrey after this book. She's an awful, misogynistic writer whose books are formulaic and, at least in my opinion, dull.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6781685560823776256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Now in this book we're supposed to accept that Robinton's mother was a renowned harper? I had a hard time getting over that MAJOR continuity issue...and the rest of the book wasn't very interesting either.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1180042804" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1180042804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11964041215427083408">Thirteenth in the chronological order for the Pern fantasy / science fiction series and revolving around dragonriders and harpers. The focus is on Robinton, a harper who goes on to greatness. The stories are a mess in following a chronological order. It's one reason I undertook a re-read of the series. Click <a href='http://kddidit.com/reading-books/chronological-lists-of-complex-intersected-series/#Pern' target='_blank' title='Opens a new page' rel='nofollow noopener'>this link</a> if you want to explore my version.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>This one is a biography which provides the background for the three primary stories of the Pern series: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1996409.Dragonflight' target='_blank' title='Opens Anne McCaffrey's Dragonflight in Goodreads' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>Dragonflight</em>
</a>, 14, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1455429.Dragonquest' target='_blank' title='Opens Anne McCaffrey's Dragonquest in Goodreads' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>Dragonques</em></a></span>
  <span id="freeText11964041215427083408" style="display:none">Thirteenth in the chronological order for the Pern fantasy / science fiction series and revolving around dragonriders and harpers. The focus is on Robinton, a harper who goes on to greatness. The stories are a mess in following a chronological order. It's one reason I undertook a re-read of the series. Click <a href="http://kddidit.com/reading-books/chronological-lists-of-complex-intersected-series/#Pern" target="_blank" title="Opens a new page" rel="nofollow noopener">this link</a> if you want to explore my version.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />This one is a biography which provides the background for the three primary stories of the Pern series: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1996409.Dragonflight" target="_blank" title="Opens Anne McCaffrey's Dragonflight in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Dragonflight</em>
</a>, 14, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1455429.Dragonquest" target="_blank" title="Opens Anne McCaffrey's Dragonquest in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Dragonquest</em>
</a>, 15, and then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1598837.The_White_Dragon" target="_blank" title="Opens Anne McCaffrey's The White Dragon in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The White Dragon</em>
</a> at 17. (The three books in the <a href="http://kddidit.com/reading-books/chronological-lists-of-complex-intersected-series/#Pern" target="_blank" title="Opens a new page" rel="nofollow noopener">Harper Hall subseries</a> take place between <em>Dragonquest</em> and <em>The White Dragon</em>.)<br /><br />It's Robinton's background, the forces that shaped him, and how he came to be Masterharper of Pern. In some ways, Robinton is the pivotal character in this last half of the series. Yes, I know that F'lar and Lessa and the dragons are the whole point of it, but it's Robinton who connects everyone on Pern, who makes Pern and the Pernese mean something to me.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I adore the dragonriders; they're what pulled me into the series in the first place, and I can't get enough about them. That said, the different factions of dragonriders have their point-of-view, there are the Lord Holders, and the craftsmen with their particular angles.<br /><br />The fostering system finds the Lords sending their sons and some daughters to other Holds to learn how that Lord handles things. Those boys who are of the Blood have the chance to become the Lord Holder when the current Lord dies because the Conclave votes in the heir they believe will be the best ruler. The girls are sent out to find husbands, which is a bit of a comedown from the crew who came in with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/465904.Dragonsdawn" target="_blank" title="Opens Anne McCaffrey's Dragonsdawn in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Dragonsdawn</em>
</a>, 1. Having a craft based in your hold is prestigious and profitable, and fortunately, the craftspeople are also autonomous. It's a relatively good system with apprentices and journeymen learning their craft, whatever it may be. Only a complacency has crept in.<br /><br />I wanna smack Petiron up one side and down the other, repeatedly. He's such a jerk. He has the most amazing son — writing compositions since he was three that the Hall has been sending out ever since. And I do adore how well the Harper Hall maneuvers around him while respecting that jerk.<br /><br />It's a good bit of history of Robinton's birth, family life, education, loves, his exposure to the various holds, and the rise of anti-Harper malice with an explanation of other characters who play roles in the coming stories, from F'lon, F'lar and F'nor's father; Camo; Sebell; the man who discovered Menolly's abilities; and, a set-up of the Lord Holders. As well as the rise of Fax, and how he got his start in conquering Pern. It's a good set-up for events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1996409.Dragonflight" target="_blank" title="Opens Anne McCaffrey's Dragonflight in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Dragonflight</em>
</a>.<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />Too many no longer believe Thread will fall and Harpers are falling into disrepute, derided, attacked, even beaten. The educators of Pern, they are being turned away from teaching the people of Pern their rights even as Fax conquers Hold after Hold, murdering as he goes.<br /><br />It's a world the colonists would never recognize on too many counts. A world Robinton is determined to save.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br />The characters range through the years, and I haven't made a distinction as to when they appear.<br /><br /><strong>Robinton</strong> is a baby being born at the start. A boy who will become the glue that holds Pern together and a brilliant musician and politician with a taste for wine and the ladies. <strong>MasterComposer Petiron</strong> is an exacting harper and Rob's father — and quite jealous of <strong>Merelan</strong>, Rob's mother and a MasterSinger, spending any time with his own son.<br /><br /><em>The Harper Hall is…</em><br />…where Pern's musicians and healers are taught and is beholden to Fort Hold. The <strong>harpers</strong> are entertainers, news broadcasters, silent diplomats, judges, and teachers. <strong>MasterHarper Gennell</strong> is the leader; <strong>Betrice</strong> is a healer and his wife; <strong>Sirrie</strong> is another healer along with <strong>Ginia</strong>, a MasterHealer. <strong>Oldive</strong> is Ginia's assistant. <strong>Washell</strong> is the Master who teaches the youngest; <strong>Kubisa</strong> is another teacher. <strong>Lorra</strong> is the cook. <strong>Master Ogolly</strong>, the Archivist, teaches musical notations and the value of the mechanics of notes. <strong>Master Bosler</strong> teaches gitar. <strong>Master Gorazde</strong> teaches drums. <strong>Severeid</strong> is another master. <strong>Nip Kinsale</strong> is Gennell's spy who, well, nips in and out to rescue people.<br /><br /><strong>Libby</strong>, <strong>Curtos</strong>, <strong>Lexey</strong> (Bosler's daughter), and <strong>Barba</strong> are more of the children; <strong>Rulyar</strong> is Searched (he becomes R'yar). <strong>Londik</strong> is senior boy soprano. <strong>Silvina</strong> is Lorra's daughter. <strong>Camo</strong> is the son Silvina bears. <strong>Saltor</strong>, the head guard, and <strong>Emfor</strong>, his burly assistant, are lent by Groghe to teach the harpers self-defense and how to hide their trail.<br /><br /><strong>Halanna</strong> is a new student from Ista Hold housed with <strong>Isla</strong>, a foster mother for students from outside the Hall. <strong>Halibran</strong> is Halanna's father; her brothers include <strong>Brahil</strong>, <strong>Landon</strong>, and <strong>Brosil</strong>.<br /><br />Apprentices in the dormitory include <strong>Shonagar</strong>, <strong>Grodon</strong>, <strong>Falawny</strong>, <strong>Shelline</strong>, <strong>Jerint</strong>, and <strong>Lear</strong> while those apprentices who progress to journeyman include <strong>Kailey</strong> and <strong>Evenek</strong>. <strong>Domick</strong> is another promising new apprentice. Traller, a.k.a., <strong>Tuck</strong>, will be a new apprentice, to Nip.<br /><br /><strong>MasterHarper Creline</strong>, the MasterHarper back when the weyrs were first found abandoned, wrote "The Question Song".<br /><br /><em>Fort Hold is…</em><br />…resided over by <strong>Lady Winalla and Lord Grogellan</strong>. <strong>Maxilant</strong> is their Harper; <strong>Grodon</strong> will follow him. <strong>Groghe</strong> is their third son. <strong>Benoria</strong> is his lady.<br /><br /><strong>Sucho</strong> and <strong>Tortole</strong> argue over who is responsible for a fallen wall. <strong>Saday</strong> is Tortole's wife; they are parents to <strong>Valrol</strong> who is married to <strong>Pessia</strong>; <strong>Torlin</strong> is a brother; and, <strong>Klada</strong> is a sister.<br /><br /><em>Benden Weyr is…</em><br />…the only weyr still occupied. <strong>S'loner</strong>, the weyerleader, rides <strong>Chendith</strong>. <strong>Carola</strong> is the Werwoman and Hayara's niece who rides <strong>Feyrith</strong>. <strong>Stolla</strong> is the headwoman. <strong>Miata</strong> handles basic lessons. <strong>T'rell</strong> is the Weyrlingmaster. <strong>Tinamon</strong> is the Healer. <strong>S'bran</strong> rides <strong>Kilminth</strong>, a bronze. <strong>Calanuth</strong>. <strong>C'gan</strong> rides blue <strong>Tagath</strong> and is their Weyrsinger. <strong>M'odon</strong> is 110 years old and rides <strong>Nigarth</strong>, a brown. <strong>Milla</strong>.<br /><br />More of the <strong>weyrlings</strong> (children born to the weyr) include <strong>Bravonner</strong> (Falloner's younger brother), <strong>Pragal</strong>, <strong>Jesken</strong>, <strong>Morif</strong>, <strong>Manora</strong>, and <strong>Larna</strong> is Carola's daughter (she'll bear F'lon a son, <strong>Fallarnon</strong>).<br /><br />Other weyrlings and candidates found on Search who impress Feyrith's last clutch include Lytonal from Ruatha who becomes <strong>L'tol</strong> with brown <strong>Larth</strong>; Rangul becomes <strong>R'gul</strong> with bronze <strong>Hath</strong>; Sellel impresses as <strong>S'lel</strong> with a bronze, <strong>Tuenth</strong>; Falloner (the friend Rob makes who is also S'loner's son;) becomes <strong>F'lon</strong> with bronze <strong>Simanith</strong>; and, <strong>Jora</strong> impresses a queen, <strong>Nemorth</strong>.<br /><br />Manora will have a son with F'lon as well, <strong>Famanoran</strong>. <strong>F'lar</strong> will Impress <strong>Mnementh</strong>, a bronze while <strong>F'nor</strong> Impresses <strong>Canth</strong>, a brown. <strong>K'net</strong> rides bronze <strong>Piyanth</strong>, <strong>B'rant</strong> rides <strong>Fanth</strong>, and <strong>B'refli</strong> rides <strong>Joruth</strong>, both browns.<br /><br /><strong>G'ranad</strong> was the previous Weyrleader.<br /><br /><em>Fort Benden is…</em><br />…the only hold to still have access to dragons and their riders. <strong>Lady Hayara</strong>, his second wife, and <strong>Lord Maidir </strong>are its rulers. <strong>Raid</strong>, the oldest son, is next in line. <strong>Maizella</strong> is their oldest daughter and has the potential of a good voice; <strong>Cording</strong> will be her spouse. <strong>Hayon</strong>, <strong>Rasa</strong>, <strong>Naprila</strong>, <strong>Anta</strong>, <strong>Jonno</strong>, and <strong>Drevalla</strong> are more of their children at Benden. <strong>Evarel</strong> is harper there. <strong>Master Yorag</strong> is the Healer. <strong>Wonegal</strong> is the MasterVintner based there.<br /><br />A belligerent cothold finds <strong>Targus</strong> and his sons <strong>Sheve</strong>, <strong>Sortie</strong>, <strong>Erkin</strong>, <strong>Mosser</strong>, and <strong>Brodo</strong> hostile to Robinton, but the woman of the house, <strong>Kulla</strong>, welcomes him.<br /><br /><em>Southern Boll was…</em><br />…second. <strong>Karenchok</strong> is their Harper. <strong>Matsen</strong> is the Seaholder. <strong>Laeala</strong> helps <strong>Healer Saretta</strong> with patients. <strong>Lord Sangel</strong> is its holder. <strong>Master Sev Ritecamp</strong> is the Station Master. <strong>Dalma</strong> is one of the young mothers in the wagon train. <strong>Rochers</strong> is one of the traders.<br /><br /><em>Pierie Hold is…</em><br />…where Merelan grew up and where Gennell sends the young family. <strong>Aunt Segonia</strong> (married to <strong>Dugall</strong>) gave Merelan her first training. <strong>Rantou</strong> is a timberman who doesn't want to be a stupid when his son arrives; <strong>Carral</strong> is his pregnant wife. Then Rantou has a grandson, <strong>Sebell</strong>.<br /><br /><em>Telgar Hold is…</em><br />…one of the largest Holds. <strong>Bristol</strong> is its Harper. <strong>Lord Tarathel</strong> is its holder. <strong>Larad</strong> is up next. <strong>Vendross</strong> and <strong>Harper Falawny</strong> are his mentors. <strong>Thella</strong> is Larad's half-sister. <strong>Macester</strong> leads Robinton's escort to Ruatha.<br /><br /><em>Ruatha Hold is…</em><br />…the third oldest Hold. <strong>Lord Ashmichel</strong> is its holder; <strong>Lady Adessa </strong>is his wife. <strong>Lessa</strong> is their young daughter born when Gennell finally explains his plans for Robinton's future. <strong>Kale</strong> is Ashmichel's son; <strong>Struan</strong> is the harper at his hold. <strong>Jez</strong> is one of Kale's handlers. <strong>Donkin</strong> is a younger nephew while <strong>Lady Gemma</strong>, also of Ruathan blood, is but one of many women espoused to Fax. <strong>Lady Tela</strong> is with her at Ruatha when <strong>Jax</strong> is born.<br /><br /><em>Tillek Hold is…</em><br />…named for <strong>James Tillek</strong> and held by <strong>Lord Melongel</strong> and <strong>Lady Juvana</strong>. The<strong> MasterFisher</strong> is <strong>Captain Gostol</strong> of the <em>Northern Maid</em>; he'll be succeeded by Idarolan. <strong>Vesna</strong> is Gostol's daughter and going for her second's ticket. Melongel has nine children including <strong>Oterel</strong>; <strong>Kasia</strong> is Lady Juvana's youngest sister. <strong>Holder Bourdon</strong> and his spouse, <strong>Brashia</strong>, are Kasia and Juvana's parents. <strong>Minnarden</strong> is its Master Harper; <strong>Mumolon</strong> and <strong>Ifor</strong> are his journeymen. <strong>Clostan</strong> is the Hold Healer with an excellent sense of dress and fit which he passes on to Robinton. <strong>Valden</strong> will take over a new hold in a forest. <strong>Kalem</strong> is a journeyman shipbuilder. <strong>Emry</strong> manages a Storage and Shipping hold. <strong>Merdine</strong> aims to be a ship's captain. I think <strong>Marlifin</strong> is an artist. <strong>Chochol</strong> is a worried holder.<br /><br /><strong>Captain Gifflen</strong> and <strong>Kepiru</strong> are two of Fax's minions.<br /><br /><strong>Captain Idarolan</strong> of <em>Wave Eater</em> and his second mate and wife, <strong>Lissala</strong>, rescue the young couple. <strong>Ellic</strong> is one of the crew.<br /><br /><em>Nerat Hold is…</em><br />…another of the holds where Robinton is sent.<br /><br /><em>Bitra Hold is…</em><br />…held by <strong>Lord Sifer</strong>.<br /><br /><em>Igen Hold has…</em><br />…<strong>Lord Tesner</strong> as its grumpy holder.<br /><br /><em>High Reaches Hold is…</em><br />…where Journeyman Robinton is sent to <strong>Master Lobirn</strong>. <strong>Lotricia</strong> is Lobirn's wife. <strong>Mallan</strong> is another Journeyman and born at High Reaches. <strong>Murfytwen</strong> holds at Murfy Hold. <strong>Masterminer Furlo</strong> works mainly copper there. <strong>Faroguy</strong> is the Lord Holder with his<strong> Lady Evelene</strong>. <strong>Fax</strong> is one of Faroguy's nephews with a profitable holding, gained by whippings and threats of eviction. Fargouy's sons, <strong>Farevene</strong> and <strong>Bargen</strong>, have been warned. <strong>Sitta</strong>, <strong>Triana</strong>, and <strong>Marcine</strong> are young ladies with whom Robinton dances.<br /><br /><em>Crom Hold is…</em><br />…held by <strong>Lord Lesselden</strong> and <strong>Lady Relna</strong>. Evenek is to be their harper but not to teach any harper nonsense. <strong>Germathen</strong> is the healer who steps in when he is beaten almost to death.<br /><br /><strong>MasterSmith Fandarel</strong> withdraws all Masters from the contested seven Holds, and other Craftmasters followed.<br /><br /><strong>Thread</strong> is a tangle of starving organisms that fall from the sky and devour anything organic in its path. <strong>Klah</strong> is a type of coffee. <strong>Fellis</strong> is a pain reliever made from a plant. To be <strong>Searched</strong> is to be chosen to try to <strong>Impress</strong> a dragon. The <strong>Charter</strong> is similar to our Constitution with the rights of all laid out. <strong>Holders</strong> are expected to allow harpers to teach all their tenants their rights. <strong>Shipfish</strong> are dolphins.<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />The cover has an orange sky with a paler orange sun and a blue dragon ready to spring off the cliff on which he's perched. I suspect it's C'gan on Tagath's back with Master Robinton standing inside a swirl of Tagath's tail, a glass of Benden white in one hand, a harp in another, and a wine bottle and another glass sitting on the clifftop in front of him.<br /><br />The title introduces the pivotal man in the core of the series, <em>The Masterharper of Pern</em>.</span>

<div id="review_803699981" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/803699981" />
    <a title="Casey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4966254-casey"><img alt="Casey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405278064p2/4966254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/803699981?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Casey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Casey" href="/user/show/4966254-casey">Casey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345388230" href="/book/show/529827.MasterHarper_of_Pern">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4966254-casey?shelf=1990s">1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4966254-casey?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4966254-casey?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4966254-casey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer803699981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9940011659430730324">MasterHarper of Pern showed improvement in plotting and characterization compared to the few books published prior. I think this was largely helped by the fact that it's a prequel to Dragonflight, so all of the big plot elements have already been established.<br/><br/>Robinton is a major character found in the first few Pern novels and any story that takes place in the Ninth Pass timeline of Pern. He's the MasterHarper, in charge of Harper Hall, has a fondness for red wine and friendship, and is a talente</span>
  <span id="freeText9940011659430730324" style="display:none">MasterHarper of Pern showed improvement in plotting and characterization compared to the few books published prior. I think this was largely helped by the fact that it's a prequel to Dragonflight, so all of the big plot elements have already been established.<br /><br />Robinton is a major character found in the first few Pern novels and any story that takes place in the Ninth Pass timeline of Pern. He's the MasterHarper, in charge of Harper Hall, has a fondness for red wine and friendship, and is a talented and beloved leader. MasterHarper of Pern provides background on his upbringing and the events leading up to Lord Fax's invasions in the northern holds of Pern, detailed in the beginning of Dragonflight.<br /><br />This is a character that never seemed particularly divisive among fans, considering other characters of Pern have gotten criticized for their more traditional treatment of women. <br /><br />About half of the book details Robinton's youth, primarily focused on his poor relationship with his father, Petiron. He is very close with his mother, Merelan. I got Freudian echoes in many of the scenes between Robinton and Merelan. I am highly doubtful McCaffrey intended anything in that manner, but their mother-son relationship felt off to me.<br /><br />Additionally, I got the impression that Petiron didn't like Robinton because he wanted Merelan all to himself, whereas later in the book it tries to frame it as Petiron was jealous of Robinton's musical abilities. Petiron didn't really act that way. Didn't try to sabotage Robinton's musical abilities or career. It was also weird how Robinton and Petiron all of a sudden came to terms in one paragraph.<br /><br />The latter half of the book has Robinton's first serious romance, with Kasia, and his dealings as a journeyman harper. The dragon rider F'lon (father to F'lar and F'nor of Dragonflight) is friends with Robinton since youth, and he pops in and out of the storyline.<br /><br />Eventually, Robinton does become MasterHarper, but it's close to the end. The last parts of this book run parallel to Dragonflight. In one way, it was interesting to have a different pov of the Ruathan Hold scene, but on the other hand, seemed way too convenient because it didn't need much originality.<br /><br />Overall, I though the pacing was better that Dragonseye and The Dolphins of Pern. Probably because it was truly focused on Robinton, and in general Robinton tends to be involved in a lot of politics and interesting events.<br /><br />Because much of this plot is already established, many of the elements don't have any surprise. We know Robinton will become MasterHarper and we know what will happen to Fax. We also know Thread is going to return. It doesn't give a whole lot of originality, but I liked reading about Robinton.<br /><br />There were some scenes early in the book, with Halanna, a young singer, that didn't sit so right with me. I chalk it up to McCaffrey's old-fashioned ideas about how to deal with strong-willed women that's pervaded the whole series, even though in the later published books it has lightened up. Essentially, Halanna is being a brat. Petiron slaps her. She calls her dad and brothers because she's mad, and then her dad spends three days hitting her until she decides to act right, and her brothers agree that's the only way to make her behave.<br /><br />Lastly, MasterHarper of Pern reneges on prior world-building when it comes to women as harpers. Robinton's mother is a MasterSinger, and there are multiple women acting as harpers. However, over about two generations, all the women have disappeared, at the start of the ya Harper Hall trilogy featuring Menolly. There's a few sloppy excuses: Robinton tried to find girls but couldn't, and an older female harper just wanted to attend to domestic duties. Considering Harper Hall fights to save traditions, it doesn't make sense. Why break with the world-building for this book?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9940011659430730324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_107652441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107652441" />
    <a title="Cass" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3891953-cass"><img alt="Cass" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295560151p2/3891953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107652441?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cass" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cass" href="/user/show/3891953-cass">Cass</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3891953-cass?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3891953-cass?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3891953-cass?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3891953-cass?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107652441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11161809771397079981"><i>The Masterharper of Pern</i> by science fiction queen <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey' title='Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anne McCaffrey</a> is one of her best works. She tells the life story of the great Masterharper Robinton, from his troubled childhood to his musical genius. He is a favourite character in the Pern series.<br/><br/>Would it be wrong of me to hijack my own review and compare the way Anne writes about Robinton with the way her son writes about his own favourite character Kindan. Anne has passed the storywriting baton to her son <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1948907.Todd_McCaffrey' title='Todd McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Todd McCaffrey</a> who has (imo) mutila</span>
  <span id="freeText11161809771397079981" style="display:none"><i>The Masterharper of Pern</i> by science fiction queen <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey" title="Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne McCaffrey</a> is one of her best works. She tells the life story of the great Masterharper Robinton, from his troubled childhood to his musical genius. He is a favourite character in the Pern series.<br /><br />Would it be wrong of me to hijack my own review and compare the way Anne writes about Robinton with the way her son writes about his own favourite character Kindan. Anne has passed the storywriting baton to her son <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1948907.Todd_McCaffrey" title="Todd McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Todd McCaffrey</a> who has (imo) mutilated Pern. One of his worse characters is Kindan, who permeates every single book written by Todd, not unlike how Robinton permeates the books written by Anne.<br /><br />This book allows us to see the natural talents of this leading man, allows us to understand why so many men and women put so much faith in him and love him so much. Anne also shows restraint, she hints that Robinton could have been a dragon rider but leaves us to dream. Compare this to Todd who put his own Kindan on the hatching grounds three times and cannot resist making him weryling master and involves him in a mating flight despite never impressing a dragon.<br /><br />Another top notch book by Anne McCaffrey.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11161809771397079981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1296270-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1215112093p2/1296270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63356295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9884289775071103848">McCaffrey offers a prelude to her original Dragonrider novels by revisiting a main character of those stories, Masterharper Robinton. However this might be more interesting if he was more of a protagonist and less of an observer to events happening about Pern. This sort of treatment cumulates at the end of the book when Robinton finds himself present to one of the most important scenes of the entire series, a Forest Gump like insertion into the storyline. An ok story, but could have been so much</span>
  <span id="freeText9884289775071103848" style="display:none">McCaffrey offers a prelude to her original Dragonrider novels by revisiting a main character of those stories, Masterharper Robinton. However this might be more interesting if he was more of a protagonist and less of an observer to events happening about Pern. This sort of treatment cumulates at the end of the book when Robinton finds himself present to one of the most important scenes of the entire series, a Forest Gump like insertion into the storyline. An ok story, but could have been so much more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9884289775071103848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Aishuu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38410238-aishuu"><img alt="Aishuu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419983957p2/38410238.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1146247296?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aishuu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aishuu" href="/user/show/38410238-aishuu">Aishuu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38410238-aishuu?shelf=read-perm-collection-hardcover">read-perm-collection-hardcover</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1146247296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17324184596330743350">I'm rereading the Pern books because I was nostalgic. This book remained in my collection, but I still can't give it a great review. As much as I love Robinton, this book is the ultimate retconn.<br/><br/>As I've been rereading Pern, the inconsistencies (and typos and name issues!) really began to bother me. I had to wonder who the heck was editing, because there was no cross-checking, and things just don't fit together right.<br/><br/>I liked this book, but I have to consider it a fanfic of Pern rather than direct</span>
  <span id="freeText17324184596330743350" style="display:none">I'm rereading the Pern books because I was nostalgic. This book remained in my collection, but I still can't give it a great review. As much as I love Robinton, this book is the ultimate retconn.<br /><br />As I've been rereading Pern, the inconsistencies (and typos and name issues!) really began to bother me. I had to wonder who the heck was editing, because there was no cross-checking, and things just don't fit together right.<br /><br />I liked this book, but I have to consider it a fanfic of Pern rather than direct canon. It doesn't fit with the rest of the series. I'm sure other people have pointed out issues, but these were the ones that really threw me out of the story:<br /><br />*Petiron - There's no way the kindly old harper from the Harper Hall books could have come from him. Aside from him saying their were no girl harpers (surprising, since he's so into female singers), Shonagar says that he can't do voice training... which is a major part of this arc. And so forth and so forth....<br /><br />*Sebell - Twenty years too early for him. In HH, it's frequently mentioned that he just walked the tables when he meets Menolly, which he becomes a journeyman about twenty years before.<br /><br />*Timeline inconsistencies galore. There's a lot that's been shoehorned in to make Robinton the center of attention, but it doesn't work when compared to any of the books written previously.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17324184596330743350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492185589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17946848669733421777">This book covers a lot of ground. It's interesting to see what pieces of Robinton's life McCaffrey zeroes in on and what pieces she summarizes -- unfortunately because it starts so early with Robinton's birth, there is quite a lot of summary.<br/><br/>I enjoyed this read, for sure, but there is a part of me that almost feels a little bit like Robinton might have been better served by the pre-existing mystery. Some characters, like Boba Fett (and Darth Vader) in Star Wars, lose some of their magic when we </span>
  <span id="freeText17946848669733421777" style="display:none">This book covers a lot of ground. It's interesting to see what pieces of Robinton's life McCaffrey zeroes in on and what pieces she summarizes -- unfortunately because it starts so early with Robinton's birth, there is quite a lot of summary.<br /><br />I enjoyed this read, for sure, but there is a part of me that almost feels a little bit like Robinton might have been better served by the pre-existing mystery. Some characters, like Boba Fett (and Darth Vader) in Star Wars, lose some of their magic when we know too much about them, and I can't help but feel, a little bit, that this holds true for Robinton, too.<br /><br />But then, the Wunderkind has never been my favorite trope. (see also my hatred for Wesley Crusher.)</span>

<div id="review_292019562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292019562" />
    <a title="Brendan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5467659-brendan"><img alt="Brendan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436833258p2/5467659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292019562?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brendan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brendan" href="/user/show/5467659-brendan">Brendan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292019562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5116234133057945501">I normally like the Pern books, but this one fell sort of flat for me. The core drama revolves around the harpers and a particularly greedy man named Fax, who starts gobbling up Holds. There's very little to do with the dragonriders, although they do appear occasionally, and much time is spent on the main character's poor relationship with his father. Love interests also die surprisingly quickly, making it hard to care about them as characters or feel any involvement in the relationships.<br/><br/>It's a </span>
  <span id="freeText5116234133057945501" style="display:none">I normally like the Pern books, but this one fell sort of flat for me. The core drama revolves around the harpers and a particularly greedy man named Fax, who starts gobbling up Holds. There's very little to do with the dragonriders, although they do appear occasionally, and much time is spent on the main character's poor relationship with his father. Love interests also die surprisingly quickly, making it hard to care about them as characters or feel any involvement in the relationships.<br /><br />It's a serviceable book, it just doesn't feel much like a Pern book, as nearly all of the plot could happen just as well anywhere.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5116234133057945501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3357740574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3357740574" />
    <a title="Michelle M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42506425-michelle-m"><img alt="Michelle M" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3357740574?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle M" href="/user/show/42506425-michelle-m">Michelle M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3357740574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1240771969758995613">6/6 <br/>3rd or 4th read. I love Robinton. <3 He /IS/the MasterHarper Of Pern<br/><br/>EDIT: (Same day as review)<br/>I feel as though I need to add this edit after reading some of the other reviews, some of which are almost 2 decades old and there would be no point in replying directly to them. <br/>1. someone mentioned A "love triangle" between Robinton, his father Petiron, and his mother Merelan. This is wrong (on so many levels). Robinton's birth was a difficult one. It almost killed Merelan. Many of the other harpe</span>
  <span id="freeText1240771969758995613" style="display:none">6/6 <br />3rd or 4th read. I love Robinton. &lt;3 He /IS/the MasterHarper Of Pern<br /><br />EDIT: (Same day as review)<br />I feel as though I need to add this edit after reading some of the other reviews, some of which are almost 2 decades old and there would be no point in replying directly to them. <br />1. someone mentioned A "love triangle" between Robinton, his father Petiron, and his mother Merelan. This is wrong (on so many levels). Robinton's birth was a difficult one. It almost killed Merelan. Many of the other harpers say that Petiron is possessive of Merelan. He only writes music that she can sing. All his music is to show off her voice. Petiron doesn't like Rob because Rob amost took away the one person that Petiron loved the most. This happens with a lot of parents whose wives die in childbirth, they reject the child that "stole" their love. Merelan ended up being sickly after Rob's birth and remained so for the rest of her life (tiring quickly, not always able to sing the complex music as often). When she dies Petiron tells Rob to "get out, you wouldn't understand" to which Rob replies "I know exactly what you're feeling" because Rob's own wife died (somewhat recently). But Petiron only cared for Merelan, not the doings of his son. <br /><br />2. Menolly being the "first" female harper being stolen by Merelan. I think what some forget is this book spans 50+ years with very little noting of that fact. Which is the biggest drawback of the book; no clear marking of time (chapter headings, for example, which became standard after Thread began to fall). In one chapter Rob's wife dies, in the next F'lar and then F'nor are born, then the next they're ready to stand for a Hatching. No joke, it seemed like Rob's wife had JUST died when there was a line "it had been 10 years since Kasia died." TEN YEARS reduced to one sentence so we could get to the "good stuff" of F'ar nad F'nor impressing their dragons. Merelan had already been dead at this time (and Petiron asking to be sent to Half-Circle Sea Hold). <br /><br />So 10 years + another 15 give or take until F'lar kills Fax. Almost 30 years since a female had gone to the Harper Hall to become a full-fledged Harper. There had been other girls (daughters of Holders) who were sent to the Hall in Rob's youth and early adulthood, but they were only sent there to learn how to sing and to memorize the teaching songs so they could teach the children of their holds. Rob asks one of the girls to come back to complete her mastery, but she refuses because she's pregnant and would rather be a Holder wife than a Harper. There was also a throwaway line about "fathers don't want to send their daughters to be harpers". Merelan had been the ONLY female masterharper (Master Singer technically) before Menolly came. And Menolly didn't just go to the Hall to become a singer/work on her voice. She went to become a Master because music was in her soul. Menolly became the first female harper in a generation. Most of the people who knew (or would have heard of/would have heard sing) MasterSinger Merelan had died by the time Menolly comes to the Hall. <br /><br />These are the only two I can remember at the moment. I may come back to edit again. <br /><br />While I really did love this book, I think it suffers from the short length and how time is severely sped up towards the end. Almost 20 Turns reduced to 50-odd pages. Which makes it seem like no time at all has passed (because nothing of importance really happens during that time). Definitely read this AFTER you finish the "main" story line that begins in DragonFlight. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1240771969758995613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2538083823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2538083823" />
    <a title="xjm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75925423-xjm"><img alt="xjm" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2538083823?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="xjm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="xjm" href="/user/show/75925423-xjm">xjm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6643048-the-masterharper-of-pern">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2538083823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1881880253426591798">It's hard to give a Pern book a low rating, but this book... really isn't all that good. It reads like mediocre Pern fanfic. Actually, I think I wrote better Pern fanfic when I was nine.<br/><br/>McCaffrey's work always had its little lumps. Her prose isn't particularly stunning (<i>Dragonflight</i> especially is rough around the edges). Details and endings are often a bit saccharine. Conflicts are a bit melodramatic and villains are a bit shallow (Fax, Kylara, Meron, Pona, Toric, Avril Bitra...) The retelling o</span>
  <span id="freeText1881880253426591798" style="display:none">It's hard to give a Pern book a low rating, but this book... really isn't all that good. It reads like mediocre Pern fanfic. Actually, I think I wrote better Pern fanfic when I was nine.<br /><br />McCaffrey's work always had its little lumps. Her prose isn't particularly stunning (<i>Dragonflight</i> especially is rough around the edges). Details and endings are often a bit saccharine. Conflicts are a bit melodramatic and villains are a bit shallow (Fax, Kylara, Meron, Pona, Toric, Avril Bitra...) The retelling of the same events in different books gets old; I'm pretty sure there are two books about every major event. And of course there are little continuity flaws here and there. (I forgave Moreta's Ride being different in <i>Moreta</i> than in the original trilogy because it's quite believable in-world that the characters of the 9th Pass would get the details wrong after 1000 years, but little things like T'Kil somehow being given a rider honorific at birth and Menolly being given a retcon 10th fire lizard were minor irritants for me even as a child.)<br /><br />But the works overall usually more than make up for these things: the fantastic worldbuilding balances out run-of-the-mill prose, villains at least <i>have</i> motivations beyond Just Being Evil, and I'll gladly put up with minor continuity issues for Pern's otherwise mind-blowing, century-spanning time travel story arcs.<br /><br />This book is not like that. It's all of the flaws and none of the awesome. The plot is as boring as the writing is bad. All the characters are stock characters; all the plot points are tropes. <br /><br />The worst for me is that the continuity errors against the rest of the canon are utterly jarring. Most major characters bear no resemblance to the people they are later in the series, in ways that no character development could account for. The Charter was rediscovered in <i>All The Weyrs of Pern</i>, and <i>The Skies of Pern</i> hinges on it having been forgotten, yet somehow is known in detail to harper and holder alike here in the 8th Interval. Robinton was always startled when dragons addressed him and dragons bespeaking him is crucial to the climax of <i>All The Weyrs</i>, yet here he's been having banal conversations with every damn dragon since age 5. Most disappointingly: sexism and gender inequality are huge themes of the series, and the gradual dismantling of gender barriers in different parts of society is a major development overall and central to the character arcs for Lessa, Menolly, Mirrim, Jancis, etc... yet somehow here, 50 years earlier, we have female harpers, female holders, female craftswomen.<br /><br />Also, ugh, the names. Honorifics are formed differently than in the rest of the series. Lytol has somehow acquired an extra syllable. Every new character is Krv'thunprononunceable or Randomsyllableth.<br /><br />Yeah. Meh. I don't think I would have liked this book even back when I spent so many childhood days drawing fire lizards and writing Impression stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1881880253426591798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2549028350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2549028350" />
    <a title="Hanneke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78109870-hanneke"><img alt="Hanneke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531052832p2/78109870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2549028350?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hanneke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hanneke" href="/user/show/78109870-hanneke">Hanneke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78109870-hanneke?shelf=dragon">dragon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2549028350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9006576253393532849">Anne McCaffrey knows how to write a story that reads away easily and this book is no exception.<br/>Still... is a must-read in the world of Pern? Not in my opinion.<br/><br/>In this book we read about a well loved character Robinton, the Masterhaper of Pern. I loved his character in the other books, and therefor was looking forward to read more about him. <br/>And although it was an easy read, it was not a fullfilling read. It was all just.... plain.<br/><br/>I read Pern for the dragons! And would have loved to read more abo</span>
  <span id="freeText9006576253393532849" style="display:none">Anne McCaffrey knows how to write a story that reads away easily and this book is no exception.<br />Still... is a must-read in the world of Pern? Not in my opinion.<br /><br />In this book we read about a well loved character Robinton, the Masterhaper of Pern. I loved his character in the other books, and therefor was looking forward to read more about him. <br />And although it was an easy read, it was not a fullfilling read. It was all just.... plain.<br /><br />I read Pern for the dragons! And would have loved to read more about the relations between Weyr, Hall and Hold. Get to read more about the dragons! There is after all a big gold one on the cover. But we do not get that, although we do get an enjoyable -plain I will say it again- book.<br /><br />Why the 2 stars and not 3? Did I mention I found it a plain story? Well that ofcourse. Also I am not a big fan of repetition. And the last 70 pages or so is almost a repetition of Dragonflight but from a different set of eyes. It is a good story (a well loved story by me), but still... repetition! If I want that story, I take that book and it does not add anything to the story of the Masterharper.<br /><br />--SPOILERS IN THE NEXT PART-<br /><br />So we read that the childhood of Robinton was not as bad as some, and not as good as some. A father that did not want to share the attention of his wife with his (newborn) son. A hall full of masters that loved and adore this young child and the potention that is in him. Not a bad deal, could have traded worst. We read about how Robinton learned the trade of Harper, who his masters were (alot of names there), in which Hold he played (again alot of names) and how he traveled there.<br /><br />We learn about his good relations with... almost everybody except the ones we hate and despite ourself (like Fax). We bond over the tragedy that overtakes Robinton when he loses his wife (again we knew something like this would happen, since there is no mention of a wife in other books).<br /><br />We learn a lot about the live of Robinton, but after reading it I can conclude that I had not missed out on any vital information all those years (and all those other books). I would have rater read about F'nol or the Weyr before Dragonflight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9006576253393532849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
