<div id="review_2132272067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2132272067" />
    <a title="Jeff Suter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24951864-jeff-suter"><img alt="Jeff Suter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382529144p2/24951864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2132272067?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff Suter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff Suter" href="/user/show/24951864-jeff-suter">Jeff Suter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12356196-the-masterharper-of-pern">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2132272067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8669469690009169520">This should have been a wonderful book, it's about Robinton one of the most likeable characters in the Pern books. But I am sorry to say Anne McCaffrey blew it big time. Of course this was at the height of the publish anything with "Dragon" in the title mania. It wouldn't be so bad if McCaffrey stayed true to her own plots and continuity. With Masterharper she totally destroys plot and continuity. <br/><br/>Continuity glitch #1: Robinton's mother is a Harper? Since when? Remember Menolly? - She was a sham</span>
  <span id="freeText8669469690009169520" style="display:none">This should have been a wonderful book, it's about Robinton one of the most likeable characters in the Pern books. But I am sorry to say Anne McCaffrey blew it big time. Of course this was at the height of the publish anything with "Dragon" in the title mania. It wouldn't be so bad if McCaffrey stayed true to her own plots and continuity. With Masterharper she totally destroys plot and continuity. <br /><br />Continuity glitch #1: Robinton's mother is a Harper? Since when? Remember Menolly? - She was a shameful thing, a girl that played music. A disgrace, an aberration - GIRLS COULDN'T BE HARPERS. The shame was so bad that Menolly's own mother tried to stop her playing ability by trying to ensure her wounded hand would not heal properly thus stopping her playing the guitar. <br /><br />Glitch#2 (And the most glaring). As a youth Robinton can talk to dragons, any dragon. This is a big deal, it is established in Dragonquest that this is a rare gift and usually confined to Weyrwomen. In Dragonquest Lessa tells Robinton that only two people on Pern can talk to any dragon, herself and Brekke. It is a very useful trait that would have aided F'Lar and Lessa in their plans to save Pern. Only Robinton seems to have "forgotten" that he can do this. He hears dragons, but thinks it is human voices. In the White Dragon, the dragons all speak directly to Robinton to stop him dying from his heart attack. Robinton is surprised about this. Now also remember that Pernese people are in awe of dragons, everyone dreams of being a dragonrider. Everyone wants to talk and be linkd to those magnificent creatures. Even owning a fire lizard is an unrequited wish. Yet Robinton has forgotten his ability to commune with dragons. I wouldn't, would you?<br /><br />Masterharper of Pern is a very flawed book. I think the 2 stars I gave it is over-generous. I only consider the three main titles and the YA parallel series (Menolly/Piemur) to be canon, all the rest can be safely ignored, especially Masterharper of Pern.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8669469690009169520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2313925029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2313925029" />
    <a title="Caroline Berg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10110379-caroline-berg"><img alt="Caroline Berg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487821880p2/10110379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2313925029?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline Berg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline Berg" href="/user/show/10110379-caroline-berg">Caroline Berg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10110379-caroline-berg?shelf=mythical-beasts">mythical-beasts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10110379-caroline-berg?shelf=music-bards-singing">music-bards-singing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10110379-caroline-berg?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10110379-caroline-berg?shelf=map-included">map-included</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2313925029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17176780779918083379">There is so much wrong with this book, and so little right. If you enjoyed Robinton as a side character, I suggest you don't read this at all, because he just doesn't work as a main character. McCaffrey seems to have an issue where anything her female characters do well, a male character (in a book written later) needs to do better and at a younger age. It's weird, but it happens with more of her characters that I care count, and doesn't do the male characters who show them up any favors either.</span>
  <span id="freeText17176780779918083379" style="display:none">There is so much wrong with this book, and so little right. If you enjoyed Robinton as a side character, I suggest you don't read this at all, because he just doesn't work as a main character. McCaffrey seems to have an issue where anything her female characters do well, a male character (in a book written later) needs to do better and at a younger age. It's weird, but it happens with more of her characters that I care count, and doesn't do the male characters who show them up any favors either.<br /><br />I feel that most of the book was really just McCaffrey wanting to go into detail about the fifty years before Lessa became Weyrwoman, and so she contrived ways to have Robinton appear at all the major turning points of history during those years. I mean, the final chapter of the book is literally the first chapter of Dragonflight, but told from a different perspective - from someone we didn't even know was there! So yeah, there is a lot of ret-conning going on too. Which isn't really fair to Robinton as a character, since he is sort of sidelined in his own book by being forced into all the history, retroactively. <br /><br />Granted, if you do want to learn about what the other Holders were like during this period on Pern, that is where this book shines. Learning about the other Lord Holders was interesting, and did make them seem more like people rather than just names tossed around. Though it is depressing to see how a small group can turn back the progressive thinking of a previous era, since it seems fifty years before Dragonflight many women were active members of the various craft halls, but with the rise of Fax all that equality just melted away.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17176780779918083379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7126273590309966431">I've recently been rereading the Pern Books and catching the ones that I originall missed. This is one of the ones that I had skipped back when it was first published as I was more interested in reading about Dragons then Harpers.<br/>Honestly, I should have passed on it this time too ... <br/>It is written somewhat biographical, somewhat 1st POV and somewhat 3rd person POV and doesn't work at all.   <span id="freeText7126273590309966431" style="display:none">I've recently been rereading the Pern Books and catching the ones that I originall missed. This is one of the ones that I had skipped back when it was first published as I was more interested in reading about Dragons then Harpers.<br />Honestly, I should have passed on it this time too ... <br />It is written somewhat biographical, somewhat 1st POV and somewhat 3rd person POV and doesn't work at all. There are many continuity and timing issues. Most noticiably is Robinton's age, you have to do some estimates based on events, which aren't really accurate in this book because of the timing issues, but it works out to be about 20+ years older then any of the original core books estimates. Sebell shouldn't even be in this story or maybe just introduced at the end as a very young new apprentice and his story is somewhat contradictory too. In Dragon Singer he has just walked the tables in the past year or two and Dragon Singer takes place 7-8 years after thread started.<br />The denouement at the end was the same exact scene that is at the beginning of Dragonflight, a scene that Robinton wasn't present for, even in disguise, in the original trilogy.<br /><br />If an original ending that pertains more to his life would have been writen or the story carried on to the beginning of thread with thread fall being the denouement and the duplicate scene being omitted, it could have redeamed this book to some extent. But that is even doubtful.<br /><br />Honestly I wouldn't have noticed most of these issues if I would have read it when it was originally published, but now that I am much more mature and reading the stories back to back, mostly in published order, the errors are glaring. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7126273590309966431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1825052753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1825052753" />
    <a title="Adrian Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41342610-adrian-rose"><img alt="Adrian Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550175761p2/41342610.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1825052753?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adrian Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adrian Rose" href="/user/show/41342610-adrian-rose">Adrian Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41342610-adrian-rose?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1825052753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5299993856542926434">In the first books of the Pern saga that were published, there is a man named Robinton, who is the Master of Harpers, the institution that is responsible for not only entertaining at festivals but also for educating the population in things like reading, arithmetic, and understanding their civil rights and responsibilities. Robinton is not a main character, but, as the story progresses, he becomes one of the best beloved of the supporting cast. This book is his story.<br/>A musical prodigy since the </span>
  <span id="freeText5299993856542926434" style="display:none">In the first books of the Pern saga that were published, there is a man named Robinton, who is the Master of Harpers, the institution that is responsible for not only entertaining at festivals but also for educating the population in things like reading, arithmetic, and understanding their civil rights and responsibilities. Robinton is not a main character, but, as the story progresses, he becomes one of the best beloved of the supporting cast. This book is his story.<br />A musical prodigy since the age of three, Robinton is the product of the marriage between a beautiful but frail soprano and a demanding, uncaring composer. He is raised in Harper Hall, the headquarters of the Harpers. As he grows, the tension between his parents leads to his being sheltered and protected by the other Harpers, and his genius going unrecognized by the man from whom he wishes approval the most. This story follows him through his life, his coming of age and tragic love, and his unwavering devotion to and friendship with the Dragonriders that protect his home from the incursions of Thread that brings devastation every couple of centuries or so. For those who know and love Pern and its heroes, this book is a must, for it answers many questions about the history of that planet that are only mentioned in passing in the other books. McCaffrey works her usual magic in creating a wonderful and endearing world full of people that the reader cannot help but fall in love with. Absolutely stunning.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5299993856542926434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2100431835" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2100431835" />
    <a title="Mick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45291025-mick"><img alt="Mick" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2100431835?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mick" href="/user/show/45291025-mick">Mick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2100431835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13276913119086060524">How can you go wrong with another installment of the original story line? This is all about good old Robinton, and takes us forward from his birth until the confrontation between F'lar and Lord Fax in Ruatha that took place in Dragonflight.<br/><br/>The hook of this story is the events, largely centered around Fax, at the end of the long turn. We start we meet many of the characters when they are young, including F'lon, father of F'lar and F'nor. Throughout the book we find out a few facts about other cha</span>
  <span id="freeText13276913119086060524" style="display:none">How can you go wrong with another installment of the original story line? This is all about good old Robinton, and takes us forward from his birth until the confrontation between F'lar and Lord Fax in Ruatha that took place in Dragonflight.<br /><br />The hook of this story is the events, largely centered around Fax, at the end of the long turn. We start we meet many of the characters when they are young, including F'lon, father of F'lar and F'nor. Throughout the book we find out a few facts about other characters we didn't know such as Camo. But those are few you to read.<br /><br />Her diction is good, as always and I added maybe 15 new words to my vocabulary. This is a fun read but I think it is enhanced by reading the other stories in the series, at least the first three centered around Benden Weyr, and then the Harperhall series centered around Menoly. Without those I think this book would have less of an impact and not be a great standalone read. Certainly enjoyed hearing the story of how Fax became what he was in Dragonflight and understanding some of the history between Fax and F'lar. The only thing I didn't like was secretly placing Robinton in Ruatha during the events. Since that was never mentioned (and would have been such a big deal) I think it was stretching my ability to suspend disbelief.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13276913119086060524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9820581561279899826">In earlier books in this series, we meet Masterharper Robinton, but what do we know of his early life? This is his story, from his birth up through the events at Ruatha Hold that lead off the first book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern___1_' title='Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, #1) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragonflight</a>. Along the way we learn about his mother, Merelan, a Mastersinger, and his father, Petiron, a Mastercomposer, and their family dynamics. From his earliest childhood Robinton is immensely musically talented — but his father never notices. In addition to the story of Robinton, this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText9820581561279899826" style="display:none">In earlier books in this series, we meet Masterharper Robinton, but what do we know of his early life? This is his story, from his birth up through the events at Ruatha Hold that lead off the first book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern___1_" title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, #1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonflight</a>. Along the way we learn about his mother, Merelan, a Mastersinger, and his father, Petiron, a Mastercomposer, and their family dynamics. From his earliest childhood Robinton is immensely musically talented — but his father never notices. In addition to the story of Robinton, this book also tells the story of Pern itself in the fifty years or so before the next Threadfall. But there are all to many who dismiss the idea that Thread will return, which leads to clashes between Hall and Hold. Multi-layered, with excellent characterization. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9820581561279899826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dA0sviMudW+f5/78Fwxq24Ma/G1XUoTTqqeb/yn2CT7XIK4cHfDlh17kmlSaQ62vsTw/W5E6/uZi9wBdCEKHNA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

The compound seemed like paradise: he could eat until he was full, and all he had to do was care for his Jouster\'s dragon, Kashet.\n\nIt didn\'t take long for Vetch to realize that Kashet was special--for unlike other dragons, Kashet was gentle by nature and did not need the tranquilizing tala plant to make her tracttable. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13127283979750134613">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br/><br/>Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br/><br/>Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High Scho</span>
  <span id="freeText13127283979750134613" style="display:none">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br /><br />Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br /><br />Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High School in Montclair, New Jersey, and graduated cum laude from Radcliffe College, majoring in Slavonic Languages and Literatures.<br /><br />Her working career included Liberty Music Shops and Helena Rubinstein (1947-1952). She married in 1950 and had three children: Alec Anthony, b. 1952, Todd, b.1956, and Georgeanne, b.1959.<br /><br />Anne McCaffrey’s first story was published by Sam Moskowitz in Science Fiction + Magazine and her first novel was published by Ballantine Books in 1967. By the time the three children of her marriage were comfortably in school most of the day, she had already achieved enough success with short stories to devote full time to writing. Her first novel, Restoree, was written as a protest against the absurd and unrealistic portrayals of women in s-f novels in the 50s and early 60s. It is, however, in the handling of broader themes and the worlds of her imagination, particularly the two series The Ship Who Sang and the fourteen novels about the Dragonriders of Pern that Ms. McCaffrey’s talents as a story-teller are best displayed.<br /><br />She died at the age of 85, after suffering a massive stroke on 21 November 2011.<br /><br />Obituaries: <a href="http://www.locusmag.com/News/2011/11/anne-mccaffrey-1926-2011/" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus</a>, <a href="http://www.mediabistro.com/galleycat/anne-mccaffrey-has-died_b42826" rel="nofollow noopener">GalleyCat</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13127283979750134613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

And there were some, like Jayge\'s trader clan, who simply preferred the freedom of the roads to the security of a hold. Others, like Aramina\'s family, had lost their holds through injustice and cruelty. For all the holdless, life was a constant struggle for survival.\n\nThen, from the ranks of the criminals and the disaffected, rose a band of renegades, led by the Lady Thella. No one was safe from Thella\'s depredations, and now her quarry was Aramina, reputed to have a telepathic link with dragons. But when Thella mistakenly vented her rage on Jayge\'s family, she made a dangerous mistake. For Jayge was bent on revenge . . . and he would never let her have the girl who heard dragons!<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"4950335287419461956\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return
